command%22%3A%22%22%2C%22poc_setup%22%3A%22%22%7D%2C%7B%22owasp_category%22%3A%22A07%22%2C%22severity%22%3A%22info%22%2C%22title%22%3A%22Weak%20password%20policy%20%E2%80%94%20single-character%20passwords%20accepted%20at%20registration%22%2C%22description%22%3A%22POST%20%2Fapi%2Fauth%2Fregister%20validates%20%60password%20%3D%3E%20'required%7Cmin%3A1%7Cmax%3A128'%60%20%E2%80%94%20one%20character%20is%20enough.%20Combined%20with%20MD5%20hashing%20the%20impact%20is%20huge%3A%20brute-forcing%20a%201-character%20MD5%20space%20is%20trivial%2C%20and%20dictionary%20attacks%20succeed%20almost%20always.%22%2C%22impact%22%3A%22%22%2C%22likelihood%22%3A%22%22%2C%22recommendation%22%3A%22Confirmed%20-%20registered%20new%20account%20with%20password%3D%5C%22a%5C%22%20(1%20char)%2C%20server%20returned%20HTTP%20201%20success.%22%2C%22cvss_score%22%3A0%2C%22cvss_vector%22%3A%22CVSS%3A3.1%2FAV%3AN%2FAC%3AL%2FPR%3AN%2FUI%3AN%2FS%3AU%2FC%3AL%2FI%3AL%2FA%3AN%22%2C%22affected_url%22%3A%22src%2FControllers%2FAuthController.php%3A11-26%22%2C%22evidence%22%3A%22%24errors%20%3D%20Validator%3A%3Amake(%24data%2C%20%5B%5C%5Cn%20%20%20%20'email'%20%20%20%20%20%20%3D%3E%20'required%7Cemail%7Cmax%3A255'%2C%5C%5Cn%20%20%20%20'password'%20%20%20%3D%3E%20'required%7Cmin%3A1%7Cmax%3A128'%2C%5C%5Cn%20%20%20%20'first_name'%20%3D%3E%20'required%7Cstring%7Cmax%3A100'%2C%5C%5Cn%20%20%20%20'last_name'%20%20%3D%3E%20'required%7Cstring%7Cmax%3A100'%2C%5C%5Cn%5D)%3B%22%2C%22request_evidence%22%3A%22%22%2C%22response_evidence%22%3A%22%22%2C%22finding_source%22%3A%22sast_lead%22%2C%22validation_status%22%3A%22confirmed%22%2C%22validation_note%22%3A%22Confirmed%20-%20registered%20new%20account%20with%20password%3D%5C%22a%5C%22%20(1%20char)%2C%20server%20returned%20HTTP%20201%20success.%22%2C%22merged_instances%22%3A%22%5B%5D%22%2C%22poc_command%22%3A%22%22%2C%22poc_setup%22%3A%22%22%7D%5D

## 1. Complete JWT signature verification bypass allows full authentication bypass and account impersonation

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A08
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/profile
- CVSS: 9.8 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H)

### Description
The API's JWT authentication mechanism (AuthService::decodeToken()) does not verify the HMAC-SHA256 signature of presented JWTs against the server's configured jwt_secret. Tokens are accepted purely based on decodable claims (e.g., exp, jti) regardless of what key was used to sign them. This was confirmed on GET /api/profile, where a JWT forged with an arbitrary, intentionally incorrect secret was accepted identically to a token signed with the real secret.

### Impact
An attacker can forge a valid-looking JWT for any user ID — customer or potentially administrative — without knowledge of any secret, and be fully authenticated as that user. This grants unauthenticated read access to profile, account, and transaction data, and enables state-changing actions (transfers, profile edits) performed as the impersonated user. This effectively removes the authentication boundary for the entire application.

### Likelihood
Certain — reproduced directly and confirmed twice: once with a real leaked secret and once with a garbage/bogus secret, both producing identical successful authentication.

### Recommendation
Fix AuthService::decodeToken() to properly verify the HMAC-SHA256 signature of the JWT against the configured jwt_secret before trusting any claim, rejecting any token whose signature does not validate. Replace hand-rolled JWT decoding with a vetted library (e.g., firebase/php-jwt) that enforces signature verification and algorithm allowlisting by default. Rotate the jwt_secret and invalidate all existing sessions after the fix is deployed.

### Evidence
```
Forged a JWT with claims {"sub":1,"user_id":1,"email":"amelia.chen@example.com","exp":9999999999,"jti":"aespa-test-jti-002"} signed with an intentionally wrong/bogus secret ("totally_wrong_secret_should_fail", not the real jwt_secret). Sending this token as Bearer auth to GET /api/profile returned HTTP 200 with the full profile data for user id=1 (amelia.chen@example.com), including the password hash, proving the HMAC signature is never verified server-side — only the exp claim and jti presence are checked.
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET /api/profile with Authorization: Bearer &lt;JWT signed with bogus secret "totally_wrong_secret_should_fail", claims sub=1,user_id=1,email=amelia.chen@example.com&gt;
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 200 {"success":true,"data":{"id":1,"email":"amelia.chen@example.com","first_name":"PWNED_BY_MASSASSIGN",...,"password_hash":"$2y$10$92IXUNpkjO0rOQ5byMi.Ye4oKoEa3Ro9llC/.og/at2.uheWG/igi",...}}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 2. Critical SSRF in /api/profile/avatar — Arbitrary URL Fetch, Local File Read via file://, and Application Source Code Disclosure

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A10:2021 Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) / API8:2023 Security Misconfiguration
- Source: specialist agent
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/profile/avatar
- CVSS: 9.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:N)

### Description
The avatar upload endpoint /api/profile/avatar accepts a user-supplied `url` parameter and passes it directly to a server-side fetch/file_get_contents-style sink with no scheme allow-listing, no host/IP validation, and no SSRF protections. Any authenticated user — including a freshly self-registered, unprivileged account — can supply arbitrary URLs, including the file:// scheme, causing the server to fetch external resources or read local files and return their contents (base64-encoded) in the API response.

### Impact
An authenticated attacker can: (1) force the server to issue arbitrary outbound HTTP(S) requests (confirmed via an external canary domain), (2) read arbitrary files on the local filesystem via file:// (confirmed by reading /etc/passwd), and (3) disclose the application's own PHP source code (confirmed by reading AdminUserController.php). The disclosed source code in turn revealed a secondary vulnerability: unparameterized SQL string interpolation in the admin customer-search feature (LIKE '%{$search}%'), corroborated by a previously observed SQL error. Beyond the confirmed proofs, this SSRF primitive could also be leveraged for internal network/port scanning, cloud metadata credential theft (AWS/GCP/Azure IMDS), and further credential/config file theft — all from a low-privilege account.

### Likelihood
High — trivially exploitable by any authenticated user, including a newly self-registered account, via a single unauthenticated-scope POST request with no special privileges required.

### Recommendation
1. Never fetch a user-supplied URL server-side without strict validation; implement an allow-list of permitted schemes (https only) and explicitly reject file://, gopher://, dict://, ftp://, etc. 2. Resolve the hostname and validate the resolved IP is not in RFC1918 private ranges, loopback, link-local (169.254.0.0/16), or other reserved ranges, and re-validate after any redirect to prevent SSRF to internal/metadata targets. 3. Remove local filesystem access from the avatar-fetch feature entirely; if remote image fetching is required, use a dedicated image-proxy service with strict content-type/size validation and no filesystem access. 4. Fix the companion SQL injection in AdminUserController::index() by using parameterized queries instead of string interpolation for the search filter. 5. Apply outbound network egress restrictions (firewall/network policies) at the host level so the application cannot reach cloud metadata services or arbitrary internal hosts even if application-layer validation is bypassed.

### Evidence
```
Request 1 (SSRF canary): POST /api/profile/avatar {"url":"https://example.com"} as freshly-registered user id=50 -> HTTP 200 with avatar_data containing base64-encoded "Example Domain" HTML, proving server-side fetch of external content. Request 2 (local file disclosure): POST /api/profile/avatar {"url":"file:///etc/passwd"} -> HTTP 200 with avatar_data decoding to full /etc/passwd contents (root, ubuntu, mysql entries). Request 3 (source disclosure): POST /api/profile/avatar {"url":"file:///var/www/bankofed/src/Controllers/AdminUserController.php"} -> HTTP 200 with base64-encoded PHP source revealing unparameterized SQL string interpolation ($where = "WHERE first_name LIKE '%{$search}%' ..."), corroborated by a prior SQLSTATE[42000] error near '%' OR last_name LIKE.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST http://100.96.0.19/api/profile/avatar
Authorization: Bearer [REDACTED_BEARER]
Content-Type: application/json

{"url": "file:///etc/passwd"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
{"success":true,"data":{"avatar_data":"data:image/png;base64,cm9vdDp4OjA6MDpyb290Oi9yb290Oi9iaW4vYmFzaAo...(truncated, decodes to full /etc/passwd contents)...","size":2089,"source_url":"file:///etc/passwd"},"message":"OK"}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 3. Critical SSRF in /api/profile/avatar Enabling Local File Disclosure via file:// Scheme

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A10
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/profile/avatar
- CVSS: 9.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N)

### Description
The avatar 'import from URL' feature at /api/profile/avatar accepts an attacker-controlled URL and fetches its contents server-side without restricting the URI scheme or destination. Supplying a file:// URI causes the server to read the target file from its local filesystem and return its full contents to the client, base64-encoded, disguised as avatar image data.

### Impact
An authenticated attacker can read arbitrary files from the application server's filesystem (source code, configuration files, credentials, private keys) via file:// URIs, as demonstrated by full disclosure of /etc/passwd. This information can be leveraged to obtain database credentials, secrets, or other sensitive configuration data, materially aiding further compromise of the server.

### Likelihood
Certain - reproduced directly, full /etc/passwd contents recovered via a single unauthenticated-style request to the endpoint.

### Recommendation
Restrict the avatar import feature to an allow-list of http(s) schemes only; explicitly disable file://, gopher://, dict://, and other non-http(s) schemes; resolve and validate that the destination IP is not private/loopback/link-local before fetching (SSRF protection); and never return raw fetched content (file or otherwise) directly to the client.

### Evidence
```
POST /api/profile/avatar with body {"url":"file:///etc/passwd"} returned HTTP 200: {"success":true,"data":{"avatar_data":"data:image/png;base64,cm9vdDp4OjA6MDpyb290Oi9yb290Oi9iaW4vYmFzaAo...","size":2089,"source_url":"file:///etc/passwd"},"message":"OK"}. Base64-decoding avatar_data reveals the full contents of /etc/passwd (root, daemon, bin, sys, mysql, ubuntu, etc.), confirming arbitrary local file disclosure via the file:// scheme. A probe of the AWS metadata service (http://169.254.169.254/latest/meta-data/) returned FETCH_FAILED, indicating no network route to that address in this environment, but the file:// vector alone constitutes a full local file read primitive.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST /api/profile/avatar {"url":"file:///etc/passwd"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 200 {"success":true,"data":{"avatar_data":"data:image/png;base64,cm9vdDp4OjA6MDpyb290Oi9yb290Oi9iaW4vYmFzaAo...(decodes to /etc/passwd contents including root, mysql, ubuntu users)...","size":2089,"source_url":"file:///etc/passwd"}}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 4. Default admin credentials (admin/admin123) grant full administrative access

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A07
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/admin/auth/login
- CVSS: 9.8 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H)

### Description
The administrative authentication endpoint at /api/admin/auth/login accepts the well-known default credential pair admin/admin123. Successful authentication returns a valid session JWT for the admin account (id: 1), providing unrestricted access to the admin panel.

### Impact
An unauthenticated attacker can log in as the primary administrator using trivially guessable credentials, gaining full administrative access to the platform including customer management, account data, FX rate configuration, and system settings. Combined with other identified issues (e.g., SQL injection in admin customer search and exposure of customer PII/financial data), this enables complete compromise of the platform and all customer data.

### Likelihood
Certain - the default credentials were reproduced successfully on the first attempt with no rate limiting, lockout, or MFA in place.

### Recommendation
Immediately disable or rotate the default admin account and enforce unique, strong passwords for all administrative accounts. Implement account lockout/rate limiting on the admin login endpoint, require multi-factor authentication (MFA) for admin access, and add monitoring/alerting for admin logins from new locations or devices. Conduct a credential audit across all environments to ensure no other default or shared credentials remain in use.

### Evidence
```
POST /api/admin/auth/login with {"username":"admin","password":"admin123"} returned HTTP 200: {"success":true,"data":{"admin":{"id":1,"username":"admin"},"token":"[JWT]"},"message":"Login successful"}
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST /api/admin/auth/login {"username":"admin","password":"admin123"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 200 {"success":true,"data":{"admin":{"id":1,"username":"admin"},"token":"[JWT]"},"message":"Login successful"}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 5. Unauthenticated Disclosure of JWT Signing Secret and Database Credentials via /api/health

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A05
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/health
- CVSS: 9.8 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H)

### Description
The /api/health endpoint is publicly accessible without any authentication and returns sensitive backend configuration values in its JSON response, including the application's JWT HMAC signing secret, the database host, database name, and database user. A simple unauthenticated GET request to this endpoint discloses this data in production.

### Impact
Possession of the JWT HMAC signing secret allows an attacker to forge arbitrary, validly-signed JWTs and impersonate any user, including administrative accounts, without needing credentials. The disclosed db_host, db_name, and db_user values further reduce the effort required to pivot to or attack the backend database (e.g., via credential stuffing, exposed database services, or chained SQL injection). Combined with any endpoint that fails to properly verify JWT signatures, this issue enables full authentication bypass across the application.

### Likelihood
Certain - a single unauthenticated GET request to a publicly reachable endpoint returns the secret and credentials with no rate limiting or access control in place.

### Recommendation
Immediately rotate the exposed JWT signing secret and database credentials. Remove all sensitive configuration values (jwt_secret, db_host, db_name, db_user, and similar) from the /api/health response and any other API response. Health/liveness endpoints should return only minimal, non-sensitive status information (e.g., {"status":"ok"}). Store secrets in a secure secrets manager or environment variables that are never serialized into API responses, and add automated tests/response schema validation to prevent regression.

### Evidence
```
Unauthenticated GET /api/health returned: {"status":"ok","php_version":"8.3.31","server":"Apache/2.4.58 (Ubuntu)","db_host":"127.0.0.1","db_name":"bankofed","db_user":"bankofed_app","jwt_secret":"Jj9XUzmBPzn8VcJEgzD9kC9koZTs1OV6XadreivDDrykIUuLimoQNqQnBdNE4Uv","environment":"production"}
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET http://100.96.0.19/api/health HTTP/1.1
```

### Response Evidence
```
{"success":true,"data":{"status":"ok","php_version":"8.3.31","server":"Apache\/2.4.58 (Ubuntu)","db_host":"127.0.0.1","db_name":"bankofed","db_user":"bankofed_app","jwt_secret":"Jj9XUzmBPzn8VcJEgzD9kC9koZTs1OV6XadreivDDrykIUuLimoQNqQnBdNE4Uv","environment":"production"},"message":"OK"}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 6. Critical BOLA on /api/transfers/external Allows Draining Any Customer's Account to an Attacker-Controlled External Account

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A01
- Source: specialist agent
- Validation: unconfirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
- CVSS: 9.8 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H)

### Description
The external transfer endpoint (backed by TransferService.php) fails to verify that the authenticated user owns the account referenced by `from_account_id` in the request body. Any authenticated user can supply an arbitrary `from_account_id` belonging to a different customer, and the server will process an external funds transfer from that account without any ownership or authorization check. Account IDs are small sequential integers, making enumeration trivial.

### Impact
Any registered, authenticated user can steal funds from any other customer's account by submitting a transfer request with that victim's `from_account_id` and their own external destination BSB/account number. This constitutes complete compromise of the platform's core financial integrity, enabling mass fraud and theft across the entire customer base with no special privileges required beyond a standard account.

### Likelihood
High — exploitation only requires a normal registered account and the ability to guess or enumerate small sequential integer account IDs; no race conditions, timing, or complex prerequisites are needed.

### Recommendation
In TransferService::externalTransfer (and the equivalent internal/own-transfer code path), load the account referenced by from_account_id and explicitly verify that account.user_id matches the authenticated user's ID before executing any debit. Reject non-owned accounts with HTTP 403. Apply the same ownership check consistently across all account-referencing endpoints (transfers, statements, address book, account details, etc.), and add automated regression tests / IDOR checks for these code paths.

### Evidence
```
Using a freshly registered low-privilege test account (user id 49, own accounts 45/47), a POST to /api/transfers/external with from_account_id=1 (belonging to a different customer, seeded with ~$999,999,999 balance) succeeded with HTTP 201, debiting account 1's balance from ~999999998.99 to 999999898.99. No ownership validation or authorization error occurred; the transfer completed and funds were routed to an attacker-specified external BSB/account (999-999 / 12345678).
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
Authorization: Bearer [REDACTED_BEARER]
Content-Type: application/json
{"amount": 100, "description": "ownership test", "from_account_id": 1, "to_account_number": "12345678", "to_bsb": "999-999", "to_payee_name": "Mule Account"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 201
{"success":true,"data":{"transaction_id":46,"from_account_id":1,"to_bsb":"999-999","to_account_number":"12345678","amount":"100","description":"ownership test","transfer_type":"manual","address_book_id":null,"totp_verified":false,"new_from_balance":"999999898.99","original_currency":null,"original_amount":null,"exchange_rate":null,"status":"completed"},"message":"Transfer completed successfully"}
```

### Validation Note
Access-control validation could not run because no alternate user sessions were available.

## 7. Critical: Server-Side TOTP Enforcement Missing on External Transfers — Client-Side-Only Control Bypass

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A01:2021 - Broken Access Control
- Source: specialist agent
- Validation: unconfirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
- CVSS: 9.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:H/A:H)

### Description
The banking application's TOTP (two-factor authentication) requirement for manual-entry (non-address-book) external transfers is enforced only by the front-end SPA and the advisory /api/transfers/check endpoint, not by the actual transfer-processing endpoint. Calling POST /api/transfers/check with transfer_type=manual returns requires_totp:true and totp_configured:false for the account, and the SPA uses this response to disable the submit button. However, POST /api/transfers/external can be called directly, without ever invoking /transfers/check and without supplying a totp_code, and the server processes the transfer to completion regardless. The response explicitly confirms totp_verified:false while status is 'completed', proving TransferService.php performs no server-side TOTP validation before executing the transfer.

### Impact
An attacker with a valid session/JWT (including accounts that have never configured TOTP) can execute external funds transfers to arbitrary destination accounts entirely bypassing the platform's two-factor authentication control, simply by calling the API directly instead of the web UI. Combined with a from_account_id authorization weakness, this could allow an attacker to move funds out of accounts without ever needing to satisfy or defeat TOTP, undermining the platform's primary anti-fraud control for high-risk transactions.

### Likelihood
High — exploitable with a single unauthenticated-of-2FA HTTP POST request; no TOTP code, prior check call, or special tooling is required.

### Recommendation
Move TOTP enforcement into the server-side transfer execution path (e.g., TransferService::externalTransfer) rather than relying solely on the advisory /transfers/check endpoint. Before completing any transfer for which risk rules require TOTP, validate a freshly issued, single-use totp_code (or equivalent verified step-up token) against the account's TOTP configuration, and reject the request with 400/403 if it is missing, invalid, expired, or already used. Ensure this check cannot be skipped by calling /transfers/external directly, and add server-side tests that verify transfers are rejected when TOTP is required but not supplied.

### Evidence
```
Step 1: POST /api/transfers/check with {"transfer_type":"manual"} returns {"requires_totp":true,"reason":"manual_entry","totp_configured":false}. Step 2: POST /api/transfers/external directly, with no totp_code and no prior check call, for the same account (totp_configured=false) returns HTTP 201 with totp_verified:false and status:"completed", proving the transfer completes despite the TOTP requirement being unmet — the control exists only in client-side logic.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
Authorization: Bearer [REDACTED_BEARER] JWT, totp_enabled:false&gt;
{"amount": 50, "description": "test bypass", "from_account_id": 45, "to_account_number": "12345678", "to_bsb": "999-999", "to_payee_name": "Mule Account"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 201
{"success":true,"data":{"transaction_id":45,"from_account_id":45,"to_bsb":"999-999","to_account_number":"12345678","amount":"50","description":"test bypass","transfer_type":"manual","address_book_id":null,"totp_verified":false,"new_from_balance":"-50.00","original_currency":null,"original_amount":null,"exchange_rate":null,"status":"completed"},"message":"Transfer completed successfully"}
```

### Validation Note
Access-control validation could not run because no alternate user sessions were available.

## 8. Unauthenticated full database export via /api/admin/export/users leaks all users, password hashes, TOTP secrets, accounts and transactions

- Severity: critical
- OWASP: A01
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: unconfirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/admin/export/users
- CVSS: 9.8 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H)

### Description
The endpoint /api/admin/export/users is an administrative bulk-export API intended to be restricted to authenticated admins, but it accepts unauthenticated GET requests. It returns a complete JSON dump of the users table (id, email, password_hash, first_name, last_name, address, phone, avatar_url, totp_secret, totp_enabled) for every user (ids 1-19+ observed), along with accounts and transactions data, with no Authorization header or session required.

### Impact
An unauthenticated attacker can retrieve the entire customer and admin dataset in a single request, including password hashes (bcrypt and legacy unsalted MD5), TOTP secrets, PII (names, addresses, phone numbers), and financial account/transaction records. This enables offline password cracking, TOTP-based MFA bypass, full account takeover of any customer or admin, and downstream fraud using the exposed transaction/account data.

### Likelihood
Certain - a single unauthenticated GET request to a known/guessable admin API path returns the full dataset with no rate limiting or access control observed.

### Recommendation
Enforce authentication and admin-role authorization (e.g., server-side session/JWT validation with role checks) on this route before any change is deployed. Remove or strictly limit bulk-export functionality; if retained, paginate/scope it to specific records, log/alert on use, and require re-authentication (step-up auth) for admins. Never include password_hash or totp_secret fields in any export or API response; exclude sensitive fields at the query/serialization layer by default. Rotate all exposed password hashes, TOTP secrets, and any credentials derivable from this dump immediately.

### Evidence
```
GET /api/admin/export/users with no Authorization header returned HTTP 200 with a full JSON dump of the users table (id, email, password_hash [bcrypt and legacy MD5], first_name, last_name, address, phone, avatar_url, totp_secret, totp_enabled) for every user (ids 1-19+ observed), plus accounts and transactions data.
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET http://100.96.0.19/api/admin/export/users HTTP/1.1 (no Authorization header)
```

### Response Evidence
```
{"success":true,"data":{"users":[{"id":1,"email":"amelia.chen@example.com","password_hash":"$2y$10$92IXUNpkjO0rOQ5byMi.Ye4oKoEa3Ro9llC/.og/at2.uheWG/igi", ...totp_secret...}, ... ]}} — status 200
```

### Validation Note
Access-control validation could not run because no alternate user sessions were available.

## 9. Missing Insufficient-Funds Check on /api/transfers/external Allows Unlimited Overdraft

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A04
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
- CVSS: 8.2 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:H/A:N)

### Description
The external transfer endpoint POST /api/transfers/external does not validate that the source account (from_account_id) holds sufficient funds before debiting it. Unlike TransferService::transferOwn(), which enforces a balance check (bccomp($fromAccount['balance'], $debitAmount, 2) < 0), the transferExternal() code path performs no equivalent check, allowing any transfer amount to be processed regardless of the account's actual balance.

### Impact
An attacker (or even a legitimate account holder) can drain an account to an arbitrary negative balance in a single request, with no credit limit, overdraft fee, or rejection logic applied. When combined with the separately identified IDOR on from_account_id (allowing transfers from accounts the authenticated user does not own), this enables unauthorized draining of victim accounts into unlimited negative balances, directly corrupting the integrity of the financial ledger and enabling fraud.

### Likelihood
Certain - reproduced directly in a single request; the API response explicitly confirms a successful transfer and a resulting negative account balance with no rejection.

### Recommendation
Add the same insufficient-funds validation used in TransferService::transferOwn() (bccomp($fromAccount['balance'], $debitAmount, 2) < 0 rejection) to TransferService::transferExternal() before debiting the source account. Ensure the check is enforced server-side for all transfer types, reject transfers that would result in a negative balance (unless an explicit overdraft/credit facility is deliberately supported with defined limits), and add regression tests covering boundary and negative-balance scenarios.

### Evidence
```
Authenticated as a disposable test user (id=51, owns no accounts), sent POST /api/transfers/external with {"amount":"50000.00","description":"balance_check_test","from_account_id":2,"to_account_number":"10000001","to_bsb":"062-001"}. Account 2 (Savings Account) had a prior balance of $18,902.00. The server responded HTTP 201 with success:true and new_from_balance "-31097.00", confirming the $50,000.00 transfer was processed with no insufficient-funds rejection, driving the account balance negative.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST /api/transfers/external {"amount":"50000.00","description":"balance_check_test","from_account_id":2,"to_account_number":"10000001","to_bsb":"062-001"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 201 {"success":true,"data":{"transaction_id":51,"from_account_id":2,"amount":"50000.00","new_from_balance":"-31097.00","status":"completed"}}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 10. Missing sufficient-funds check on /api/transfers/external allows overdraft to negative balance

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A04:2021 - Insecure Design (Business Logic Flaw)
- Source: specialist agent
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
- CVSS: 8.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:H/A:L)

### Description
The external transfer endpoint (POST /api/transfers/external) does not validate that the source account holds sufficient funds before processing a debit. Using an account with a confirmed $0.00 balance, a $50 external transfer was submitted and completed successfully, driving the account balance to -$50.00. No rejection, warning, or overdraft-fee logic was triggered, indicating the balance check is either absent or only enforced client-side.

### Impact
Any authenticated user can transfer more funds than their account actually holds, creating unauthorized negative balances and effectively unlimited, unsecured overdrafts. This exposes the bank to direct financial loss and, if combined with account enumeration or the previously identified BOLA issue, could allow an attacker to drain funds from multiple accounts beyond their actual holdings.

### Likelihood
High — trivially reproducible with any account balance and no special preconditions; confirmed with a single request in this test.

### Recommendation
In the transfer processing logic (e.g. TransferService::externalTransfer), enforce a server-side check prior to debiting that (source balance - transfer amount - any fees) is >= the account's permitted minimum (0, or an approved overdraft limit). Reject with an INSUFFICIENT_FUNDS error when the check fails, and perform the check-and-debit atomically (within a database transaction using row-level locking) to also prevent race-condition double-spend attacks.

### Evidence
```
Account 45 balance confirmed at $0.00 via GET /api/accounts prior to the transfer. A subsequent POST /api/transfers/external with amount=50 from_account_id=45 returned HTTP 201 with "success":true, "new_from_balance":"-50.00", "status":"completed" — the transfer was accepted and completed despite insufficient funds, leaving the account at a negative balance.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
Authorization: Bearer [REDACTED_BEARER] JWT&gt;
{"amount": 50, "description": "test bypass", "from_account_id": 45, "to_account_number": "12345678", "to_bsb": "999-999", "to_payee_name": "Mule Account"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 201
{"success":true,"data":{"transaction_id":45,"from_account_id":45,"to_bsb":"999-999","to_account_number":"12345678","amount":"50","description":"test bypass","transfer_type":"manual","address_book_id":null,"totp_verified":false,"new_from_balance":"-50.00","original_currency":null,"original_amount":null,"exchange_rate":null,"status":"completed"},"message":"Transfer completed successfully"}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 14. SQL Injection in /api/transactions via unsanitized `sort` parameter (ORDER BY clause)

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A03
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/transactions?sort=
- CVSS: 7.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:L/A:N)

### Description
The `sort` query parameter on the authenticated `/api/transactions` endpoint is concatenated directly into the SQL query's ORDER BY clause without parameterisation, escaping, or column-name whitelisting. Submitting SQL syntax in the parameter value alters the structure of the underlying query, as confirmed by the application's MySQL error responses.

### Impact
An authenticated user can manipulate the raw SQL statement executed against the transactions table. While confirmation here is error-based (syntax errors reflecting the injected SQL), the underlying flaw of unsanitized interpolation into the ORDER BY clause is a strong indicator that blind boolean- or time-based techniques could be used to enumerate or exfiltrate database contents beyond the caller's own records (e.g., other customers' transactions or account data), or to degrade service availability via expensive injected subqueries.

### Likelihood
Certain - reproduced twice with distinct payloads (`sort=created_at;SELECT SLEEP(3)` and `sort=(SELECT SLEEP(3))`), both returning MySQL syntax errors whose text reflects the injected SQL placed directly into the ORDER BY clause, confirming unsanitized string interpolation.

### Recommendation
Replace free-text sort input with a strict whitelist of permitted column names and directions (e.g. ['created_at','amount','id'] x ['asc','desc']), rejecting any value that does not exactly match an allowed entry. Never interpolate user-controlled input into SQL identifier or clause positions; use parameterised queries for values and a server-side lookup map for column/direction selection. Additionally, disable verbose SQL error detail in production responses.

### Evidence
```
GET /api/transactions?sort=created_at;SELECT SLEEP(3) returned HTTP 500 with SQLSTATE[42000] syntax error: "... near 'SELECT SLEEP(3) DESC LIMIT ? OFFSET ?' at line 4", confirming the injected value was placed directly into the ORDER BY clause. Identical result reproduced with sort=(SELECT SLEEP(3)).
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET /api/transactions?sort=created_at;SELECT SLEEP(3) with Authorization: Bearer &lt;valid JWT&gt;
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 500 {"error":{"code":"INTERNAL_ERROR","message":"SQLSTATE[42000]: Syntax error or access violation: 1064 ... near 'SELECT SLEEP(3) DESC LIMIT ? OFFSET ?' at line 4",...}}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 15. SQL Injection in Admin Customer Search Endpoint (`search` Parameter)

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A03
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/admin/customers?search=
- CVSS: 8.6 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:N)

### Description
The admin customer search endpoint (`GET /api/admin/customers`) concatenates the user-supplied `search` query parameter directly into a SQL `WHERE` clause without parameterisation or sanitisation. Submitting a single quote in the `search` value breaks out of the intended `LIKE` clause and causes a MySQL syntax error, confirming that attacker-controlled input reaches the SQL query unescaped. This is exploitable by any user holding a valid admin session/JWT, including one obtained via the previously identified default admin/admin123 credentials.

### Impact
An attacker with an admin-authenticated session can leverage this SQL injection to perform UNION-based extraction of arbitrary database contents, including admin credential hashes, full customer PII, and financial/account data, entirely bypassing application-level authorization and data segregation controls.

### Likelihood
Certain - directly reproduced by appending a single quote to the search parameter, which returned a distinctive MySQL 1064 syntax error reflecting the injected payload back in the query fragment, confirming unsanitised string concatenation into the SQL statement.

### Recommendation
Rewrite the customer search query to use parameterised queries (e.g., PDO prepared statements with bound parameters) instead of string concatenation/interpolation for the `search` value. Apply input validation/allow-listing as defense in depth, disable verbose SQL error messages in production, and audit other admin endpoints for the same pattern.

### Evidence
```
Authenticated as admin (admin/admin123), GET /api/admin/customers?search=test' returned HTTP 500 with SQLSTATE[42000]: Syntax error or access violation: 1064, showing the injected payload reflected in the query fragment: "... near '%' OR last_name LIKE '%test'%' OR email LIKE '%test'%'' at line 1" (error traced to /var/www/bankofed/src/Controllers/AdminUserController.php:28), confirming the search parameter is concatenated directly into the SQL WHERE clause without parameterisation.
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET /api/admin/customers?search=test' with Authorization: Bearer &lt;admin JWT&gt;
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 500 {"error":{"code":"INTERNAL_ERROR","message":"SQLSTATE[42000]: Syntax error or access violation: 1064 ... near '%' OR last_name LIKE '%test'%' OR email LIKE '%test'%'' at line 1",...}}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 16. Stored Cross-Site Scripting via Unsanitized Transfer `description` Field (Cross-User, Admin-Reachable)

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A03
- Source: specialist agent
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
- CVSS: 8.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:R/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:N)

### Description
The `description` field accepted by POST /api/transfers/external is stored verbatim in the database without server-side sanitization or output encoding. Because external transfers allow any authenticated low-privilege user to specify an arbitrary target BSB/account number, an attacker can plant an HTML/JavaScript payload directly into a victim's transaction history without any prior relationship or interaction from the victim. The stored value is later rendered via unsafe `innerHTML` sinks in the front-end (dashboard.js `renderTransactions`, accounts.js `renderDetailTransactions`), executing the injected script whenever the victim or a bank admin views the affected account/transaction. Other transaction fields such as `original_currency` and `tx.type` are already passed through `U.escapeHtml()` in the same rendering functions, confirming that `description` is the outlier that was missed.

### Impact
An attacker with only a self-registered account can achieve persistent, cross-user XSS against any other customer's transaction history simply by initiating an external transfer with a malicious description, requiring no action from the victim beyond normal use of the site. When the victim (or an admin reviewing the transaction in the admin console) loads the affected dashboard/account page, the injected script executes in their authenticated session, enabling theft of the JWT stored in localStorage (`bankofed_token`), full account takeover, or initiation of fraudulent transactions on the victim's behalf.

### Likelihood
High — exploitation requires only a standard registered account and knowledge of a target BSB/account number; no social engineering or victim interaction is needed to deliver the payload, and the payload was confirmed to be stored unescaped and reachable via a real third-party account in this test.

### Recommendation
Sanitize/validate the `description` field server-side at write time (reject or strip HTML/script content), and consistently HTML-encode it at render time using the existing `U.escapeHtml()` helper in all client-side templates that render transaction data (dashboard.js, accounts.js), matching the treatment already applied to `original_currency` and `tx.type`. Additionally deploy a restrictive Content-Security-Policy as defense in depth to limit the impact of any future injection.

### Evidence
```
POST /api/transfers/external with body containing `"description":"<svg/onload=alert(document.cookie)>"` targeting a real third-party account (BSB 062-003 / Acc 30000001) returned HTTP 201 with the payload stored verbatim in the response: `"description":"<svg\/onload=alert(document.cookie)>"` (transaction_id 49). This confirms the payload is persisted on the victim's transaction history and will execute via the vulnerable innerHTML rendering sinks when viewed by the victim or an admin.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/external
Authorization: Bearer [REDACTED_BEARER] JWT>
Content-Type: application/json

{"amount": 0.01, "description": "<svg/onload=alert(document.cookie)>", "from_account_id": 46, "payee_name": "Amelia Chen", "to_account_number": "30000001", "to_bsb": "062-003"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
{"success":true,"data":{"transaction_id":49,"from_account_id":46,"to_bsb":"062-003","to_account_number":"30000001","amount":"0.01","description":"<svg\/onload=alert(document.cookie)>","transfer_type":"manual","address_book_id":null,"totp_verified":false,"new_from_balance":"4999.98","original_currency":null,"original_amount":null,"exchange_rate":null,"status":"completed"},"message":"Transfer completed successfully"}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 17. Stored XSS via Unsanitized Transaction `description` Field Rendered Through innerHTML

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A03
- Source: specialist agent
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/banking/#/transfers
- CVSS: 8.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:R/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:N)

### Description
The transfer functionality (`POST /api/transfers/own`) accepts an arbitrary, unsanitized `description` field and persists it verbatim server-side. This description is later returned by `GET /api/accounts/{id}` and rendered client-side by concatenating `tx.description` directly into `innerHTML` in both `banking/js/pages/dashboard.js` and `banking/js/pages/accounts.js` (`renderDetailTransactions`), with no HTML escaping applied. Notably, adjacent fields in the same template (`tx.original_currency`, `tx.type`) are explicitly passed through the application's `U.escapeHtml()` helper, confirming that `description` is the sole field missing this control and that the escaping mechanism exists but was simply not applied here.

### Impact
Any authenticated user, including a low-privilege customer, can set an attacker-controlled HTML/JS payload as a transaction description via the self-service transfer feature (own or external transfers). Because both the sender and receiver of a transaction can view it — via account statements, dashboards, and potentially admin transaction views — the payload will execute in the browser context of any other user or admin who subsequently views the affected account's transaction list. Given that the application's JWT (`bankofed_token`) is stored in `localStorage` and is therefore directly readable by injected JavaScript, this could enable session/token theft, account takeover, fraudulent transfers performed as the victim, or privilege escalation if an administrator views the malicious transaction in the admin panel.

### Likelihood
High — the injection point is reachable by any registered user through the standard transfer form/API with no elevated privileges required, and the payload was confirmed to be stored and returned unescaped by the backend. Exploitation requires a victim (another user or admin) to view the affected transaction, and requires the escaping gap identified in source review to hold at render time.

### Recommendation
Apply the same `U.escapeHtml()` sanitization already used for `original_currency`, `tx.type`, `account_name`, `bsb`, and `account_number` to `tx.description` in `dashboard.js`, `accounts.js` (`renderDetailTransactions`), and any other template that concatenates `tx.description` into `innerHTML`. Additionally, enforce output encoding/escaping server-side or adopt a templating engine with auto-escaping by default, and deploy a restrictive Content-Security-Policy to mitigate residual injection risk. As defense-in-depth, validate/sanitize the `description` field server-side at write time.

### Evidence
```
POST /api/transfers/own with description set to `<img src=x onerror=alert(document.domain)>` returned HTTP 201 with the payload stored verbatim in the response. A subsequent GET /api/accounts/48 returned the identical unescaped payload in `recent_transactions[0].description`, confirming stored persistence. Client-side source review of dashboard.js and accounts.js confirmed `tx.description` is concatenated directly into `innerHTML` without calling `U.escapeHtml()`, while sibling fields (`tx.original_currency`, `tx.type`) in the same rendering functions are explicitly escaped, demonstrating an inconsistent/missing escaping gap specific to `description`. Browser-based DOM execution proof (actual `alert()` firing) was not captured in this session, but the confirmed unescaped storage/retrieval combined with the identified unescaped innerHTML sink is conclusive evidence of exploitable stored XSS.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST http://100.96.0.19/api/transfers/own
Authorization: Bearer [REDACTED_BEARER] JWT>
Content-Type: application/json

{"amount": 0.01, "description": "<img src=x onerror=alert(document.domain)>", "from_account_id": 46, "to_account_id": 48}
```

### Response Evidence
```
{"success":true,"data":{"transaction_id":48,"from_account_id":46,"to_account_id":48,"amount":"0.01","credit_amount":"0.01","description":"<img src=x onerror=alert(document.domain)>","new_from_balance":"4999.99","new_to_balance":"0.01","original_currency":null,"original_amount":null,"exchange_rate":null,"status":"completed"},"message":"Transfer completed successfully"}

Subsequent GET /api/accounts/48:
{"success":true,"data":{"account":{...},"recent_transactions":[{"id":48,...,"description":"<img src=x onerror=alert(document.domain)>",...}]},"message":"OK"}
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 18. Stored XSS via Unsanitized Transaction `description` Field Rendered Through innerHTML

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A03
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/banking/js/pages/dashboard.js
- CVSS: 8.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:L/A:N)

### Description
The `description` field on money transfers (POST /api/transfers/external) is accepted and stored by the server without sanitization and is later rendered into the dashboard and account-detail views by direct string concatenation into innerHTML. In banking/js/pages/dashboard.js, renderTransactions() builds transaction rows using `'<p class="font-medium text-slate-900 truncate">' + (tx.description || tx.type) + '</p>'` and assigns the resulting string to `container.innerHTML`. Unlike adjacent fields in the same file (e.g., acc.account_name, acc.bsb, acc.account_number), which are passed through U.escapeHtml(), the description field is never escaped. The equivalent renderDetailTransactions() function in accounts.js follows the same unsafe pattern.

### Impact
Any authenticated user can submit a money transfer containing an HTML/JS payload in the description field. When the transaction is later viewed on the dashboard (or account detail page) by the account owner — or by any party with visibility into that transaction, including a recipient via the confirmed transfer IDOR — the payload is parsed and executed by their browser in the context of the banking application. This allows session-token theft via document.cookie, DOM manipulation of the banking UI, or CSRF-driven follow-on fraud. Because transfers can target arbitrary accounts, this is a cross-user stored XSS with potential to escalate to higher-privileged sessions if an admin or support user ever reviews the affected transaction.

### Likelihood
Certain — both the injection point and the vulnerable sink were directly confirmed: the server accepts and persists the raw payload verbatim, and the client-side source code shows the description field concatenated unescaped into an innerHTML assignment, with no client-side or server-side sanitization observed at any stage.

### Recommendation
Escape the description field before rendering: call U.escapeHtml(tx.description || tx.type) in dashboard.js renderTransactions() and the equivalent renderDetailTransactions() in accounts.js, consistent with the escaping already applied to other fields (account_name, bsb, account_number) in the same functions. Additionally, apply server-side output encoding or a strict allow-list/length validation on the description field at the /api/transfers/external endpoint, and consider adding a Content-Security-Policy to reduce the impact of any future unescaped-output regressions.

### Evidence
```
POST /api/transfers/external with description "<img src=x onerror=alert(document.cookie)>" was accepted (HTTP 201) and stored/returned verbatim by the server. Direct retrieval of banking/js/pages/dashboard.js confirmed the rendering sink: renderTransactions() concatenates `(tx.description || tx.type)` raw into an HTML string with no U.escapeHtml() call (unlike sibling fields in the same function), then assigns it via `container.innerHTML = html;`, causing any injected HTML/JS to execute in the viewer's browser.
```

### Request Evidence
```
POST /api/transfers/external {"amount":"1.00","description":"&lt;img src=x onerror=alert(document.cookie)&gt;","from_account_id":2,"to_account_number":"10000001","to_bsb":"062-001"}
```

### Response Evidence
```
HTTP 201 {"success":true,"data":{"transaction_id":52,"description":"&lt;img src=x onerror=alert(document.cookie)&gt;",...}} ; dashboard.js: '<p ...>' + (tx.description || tx.type) + '</p>' (no escapeHtml call) then container.innerHTML = html;
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 19. IDOR in transaction detail endpoint — any authenticated user can view any transaction by ID

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A01
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: unconfirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/transactions/1
- CVSS: 7.5 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N)

### Description
The transaction detail endpoint GET /api/transactions/{id} does not verify that the requesting user owns either the source or destination account of the transaction being requested. Any authenticated user can supply an arbitrary transaction ID and retrieve the full transaction record belonging to other customers.

### Impact
Any authenticated user can enumerate sequential transaction IDs (1..N) to view every other customer's transaction details, including BSB numbers, account numbers, amounts, and descriptions. This constitutes a full breach of transaction confidentiality across the customer base and could be automated to scrape the entire transaction history of the platform.

### Likelihood
Certain - reproduced directly using a newly-registered, unrelated disposable account with no relationship to the accessed transaction or its owning accounts.

### Recommendation
In TransactionController::show (and any equivalent endpoint), verify that the authenticated user owns the account referenced by from_account_id or to_account_id on the requested transaction before returning it; return 404/403 otherwise. Apply the same ownership check consistently to any endpoint that accepts a transaction, account, or user identifier from the client.

### Evidence
```
Authenticated as newly-registered user id=48 (aespa_bb688f53@example.invalid), unrelated to accounts 1/2. GET /api/transactions/1 returned HTTP 200 with full transaction detail: {"id":1,"from_account_id":1,"to_bsb":"062-001","to_account_number":"10000002","to_account_id":2,"amount":"500.00","description":"Monthly savings",...}. No ownership check was performed.
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET /api/transactions/1 with Authorization: Bearer &lt;JWT for user 48&gt;
```

### Response Evidence
```
{"success":true,"data":{"id":1,"from_account_id":1,"to_account_id":2,"amount":"500.00","description":"Monthly savings",...}}
```

### Validation Note
Access-control validation could not run because no alternate user sessions were available.

## 20. Mass-Assignment IDOR in PUT /api/profile Allows Overwriting Any User's Profile

- Severity: high
- OWASP: A01
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: unconfirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/profile
- CVSS: 8.1 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:N)

### Description
The PUT /api/profile endpoint trusts a client-supplied 'user_id' field in the request body to determine which user's profile record to update, instead of deriving the target strictly from the authenticated session/JWT. This is a broken object-level authorization (mass-assignment/IDOR) flaw that allows any authenticated user to modify another user's profile data by simply including that user's ID in the request payload.

### Impact
Any authenticated user can overwrite arbitrary profile fields (name, address, phone, email) belonging to any other user by supplying that user's user_id in the request body. If the email field can be modified through this same path, an attacker could redirect password-reset flows to an attacker-controlled address, resulting in full account takeover of any user, including privileged accounts.

### Likelihood
Certain - reproduced directly with a live request against the target API.

### Recommendation
Never trust a client-supplied user_id (or any other object identifier) in the request body for identifying the update target. Derive the target user strictly from the authenticated JWT/session on the server side, and reject or ignore any user_id field submitted in the body. Apply server-side allow-listing of updatable fields (avoid blind mass-assignment of request bodies to ORM/model objects), and add object-level authorization checks that verify the authenticated user owns the resource being modified before persisting changes. Add regression tests that attempt to update another user's profile via a spoofed user_id and confirm the request is rejected (403/404).

### Evidence
```
Authenticated as disposable user id=48, sent PUT /api/profile with body {"first_name":"PWNED_BY_MASSASSIGN","user_id":1}. Server responded HTTP 200 with the profile of user id=1 (amelia.chen@example.com) showing first_name updated to "PWNED_BY_MASSASSIGN", confirming that user 48's request modified user 1's profile rather than its own.
```

### Request Evidence
```
PUT /api/profile {"first_name":"PWNED_BY_MASSASSIGN","user_id":1} with Authorization: Bearer &lt;JWT for user 48&gt;
```

### Response Evidence
```
{"success":true,"data":{"id":1,"email":"amelia.chen@example.com","first_name":"PWNED_BY_MASSASSIGN",...},"message":"Profile updated successfully"}
```

### Validation Note
Access-control validation could not run because no alternate user sessions were available.

## 21. Outdated client-side libraries (jQuery 3.3.1, moment.js 2.29.1) with known CVEs used to render server-controlled data

- Severity: medium
- OWASP: A06
- Source: Dynamic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/banking/index.html
- CVSS: 5.9 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:L/A:N)

### Description
The banking application (http://100.96.0.19/banking/index.html) bundles/loads outdated client-side JavaScript libraries — jQuery 3.3.1 and moment.js 2.29.1. public/banking/js/pages/profile.js explicitly references the bundled jQuery 3.3.1 and uses jQuery's .html() method to inject server-returned values (avatar_data, source_url) from the Import Avatar feature directly into the DOM ($('#avatar-preview').html(...), $('#avatar-source').html(...)).

### Impact
jQuery 3.3.1 is affected by CVE-2019-11358 (prototype pollution via $.extend) and known htmlPrefilter-related XSS issues; moment.js 2.29.1 is affected by CVE-2022-24785 (path traversal in locale loading) and CVE-2022-31129 (ReDoS). Because profile.js renders externally-sourced fields (avatar_data, source_url) via .html() without sanitization, an attacker able to influence the data returned by the Import Avatar feature (see related SSRF finding) could achieve DOM-based XSS in the context of the banking application, potentially leading to session/token theft or unauthorized actions.

### Likelihood
Medium - exploitation requires a victim to load the profile page after the Import Avatar feature has processed attacker-influenced data (e.g., avatar_data or source_url); no direct social engineering beyond normal page navigation is needed, but it depends on that data reaching the vulnerable .html() sinks.

### Recommendation
Upgrade jQuery to the latest patched 3.x release (>=3.5.0) and moment.js to the latest patched release, or migrate to a maintained, actively supported alternative (e.g., date-fns, luxon for dates; native DOM APIs for jQuery). Replace .html() calls that render avatar_data/source_url with safe DOM methods (textContent, createElement) or a sanitizer such as DOMPurify. Pin and regularly update all client-side dependencies as part of an SCA/dependency-scanning process.

### Evidence
```
public/banking/js/pages/profile.js contains the comment "// jQuery-driven avatar import (uses the bundled jQuery 3.3.1)" and calls $('#avatar-preview').html(...) / $('#avatar-source').html(...) with server-controlled data (avatar_data, source_url) from the Import Avatar feature. banking/index.html loads jQuery 3.3.1 and moment.js 2.29.1, both of which have known CVEs (jQuery: CVE-2019-11358; moment.js: CVE-2022-24785, CVE-2022-31129).
```

### Request Evidence
```
GET http://100.96.0.19/banking/js/pages/profile.js
```

### Response Evidence
```
// jQuery-driven avatar import (uses the bundled jQuery 3.3.1) ... $('#avatar-preview').html('&lt;img src="' + data.avatar_data + '" ...'); $('#avatar-source').html('Imported ' + data.size + ' bytes from ' + data.source_url)
```

### Validation Note
Adversarial validator exhausted the step budget without finding a disproof.

## 24. Sensitive data exposed in API response

- Severity: medium
- OWASP: A02
- Source: Deterministic
- Validation: confirmed
- Affected URL: http://100.96.0.19/api/auth/register
- CVSS: 6.5 (CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:L/A:N)

### Description

### Impact

{"success":true,"data":{"avatar_data":"data:image\/png;base64,cm9vdDp4OjA6MDpyb290Oi9yb290Oi9iaW4vYmFzaApkYWVtb246eDoxOjE6ZGFlbW9uOi91c3Ivc2JpbjovdXNyL3NiaW4vbm9sb2dpbgpiaW46eDoyOjI6YmluOi9iaW46L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4Kc3lzOng6MzozOnN5czovZGV2Oi91c3Ivc2Jpbi9ub2xvZ2luCnN5bmM6eDo0OjY1NTM0OnN5bmM6L2JpbjovYmluL3N5bmMKZ2FtZXM6eDo1OjYwOmdhbWVzOi91c3IvZ2FtZXM6L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4KbWFuOng6NjoxMjptYW46L3Zhci9jYWNoZS9tYW46L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4KbHA6eDo3Ojc6bHA6L3Zhci9zcG9vbC9scGQ6L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4KbWFpbDp4Ojg6ODptYWlsOi92YXIvbWFpbDovdXNyL3NiaW4vbm9sb2dpbgpuZXdzOng6OTo5Om5ld3M6L3Zhci9zcG9vbC9uZXdzOi91c3Ivc2Jpbi9ub2xvZ2luCnV1Y3A6eDoxMDoxMDp1dWNwOi92YXIvc3Bvb2wvdXVjcDovdXNyL3NiaW4vbm9sb2dpbgpwcm94eTp4OjEzOjEzOnByb3h5Oi9iaW46L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4Kd3d3LWRhdGE6eDozMzozMzp3d3ctZGF0YTovdmFyL3d3dzovdXNyL3NiaW4vbm9sb2dpbgpiYWNrdXA6eDozNDozNDpiYWNrdXA6L3Zhci9iYWNrdXBzOi91c3Ivc2Jpbi9ub2xvZ2luCmxpc3Q6eDozODozODpNYWlsaW5nIExpc3QgTWFuYWdlcjovdmFyL2xpc3Q6L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4KaXJjOng6Mzk6Mzk6aXJjZDovcnVuL2lyY2Q6L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4KX2FwdDp4OjQyOjY1NTM0Ojovbm9uZXhpc3RlbnQ6L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4Kbm9ib2R5Ong6NjU1MzQ6NjU1MzQ6bm9ib2R5Oi9ub25leGlzdGVudDovdXNyL3NiaW4vbm9sb2dpbgpzeXN0ZW1kLW5ldHdvcms6eDo5OTg6OTk4OnN5c3RlbWQgTmV0d29yayBNYW5hZ2VtZW50Oi86L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4Kc3lzdGVtZC10aW1lc3luYzp4Ojk5Njo5OTY6c3lzdGVtZCBUaW1lIFN5bmNocm9uaXphdGlvbjovOi91c3Ivc2Jpbi9ub2xvZ2luCmRoY3BjZDp4OjEwMDo2NTUzNDpESENQIENsaWVudCBEYWVtb24sLCw6L3Vzci9saWIvZGhjcGNkOi9iaW4vZmFsc2UKbWVzc2FnZWJ1czp4OjEwMToxMDE6Oi9ub25leGlzdGVudDovdXNyL3NiaW4vbm9sb2dpbgpzeXNsb2c6eDoxMDI6MTAyOjovbm9uZXhpc3RlbnQ6L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4Kc3lzdGVtZC1yZXNvbHZlOng6OTkxOjk5MTpzeXN0ZW1kIFJlc29sdmVyOi86L3Vzci9zYmluL25vbG9naW4KdXVpZGQ6eDoxMDM6MTAzOjovcnVuL3V1aWRkOi91c3Ivc2Jpbi9ub2xvZ2luCnRzczp4OjEwNDoxMDQ6VFBNIHNvZnR3YXJlIHN0YWNrLCwsOi92YXIvbGliL3RwbTovYmluL2ZhbHNlCnNzaGQ6eDoxMDU6NjU1MzQ6Oi9ydW4vc3NoZDovdXNyL3NiaW4vbm9sb2dpbgpwb2xsaW5hdGU6eDoxMDY6MTo6L3Zhci9jYWNoZS9wb2xsaW5hdGU6L2Jpbi9mYWxzZQp0Y3BkdW1wOng6MTA3OjEwODo6L25vbmV4aXN0ZW
